<div id="review_80843198" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/80843198" />
    <a title="Jacqueline" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1739429-jacqueline"><img alt="Jacqueline" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578724220p2/1739429.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/80843198?book_show_action=true">Dec 13, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacqueline" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacqueline" href="/user/show/1739429-jacqueline">Jacqueline</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1739429-jacqueline?shelf=fantasy-paranormal">fantasy-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1739429-jacqueline?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1739429-jacqueline?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1739429-jacqueline?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1739429-jacqueline?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer80843198" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4972836618862558759">After reading <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4447622.Some_Girls_Bite__Chicagoland_Vampires___1_' title='Some Girls Bite (Chicagoland Vampires, #1) by Chloe Neill' rel='nofollow noopener'>Some Girls Bite</a>
</i> and it's follow-up <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6319978.Friday_Night_Bites__Chicagoland_Vampires___2_' title='Friday Night Bites (Chicagoland Vampires, #2) by Chloe Neill' rel='nofollow noopener'>Friday Night Bites</a>
</i>, I've come to adore Chloe Neill's new urban fantasy series. Not only does <i>Twice Bitten</i> continue the Chicagoland Vampires series's winning streak, it ups the ante.<br/><br/>Picking up directly where the second book left off, it's two months after Merit made the change from human to vampire and became the Sentinel of her new house, Cadogan. Although she still struggles - with lust as well as the fighting - during her physical traini</span>
  <span id="freeText4972836618862558759" style="display:none">After reading <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4447622.Some_Girls_Bite__Chicagoland_Vampires___1_" title="Some Girls Bite (Chicagoland Vampires, #1) by Chloe Neill" rel="nofollow noopener">Some Girls Bite</a>
</i> and it's follow-up <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6319978.Friday_Night_Bites__Chicagoland_Vampires___2_" title="Friday Night Bites (Chicagoland Vampires, #2) by Chloe Neill" rel="nofollow noopener">Friday Night Bites</a>
</i>, I've come to adore Chloe Neill's new urban fantasy series. Not only does <i>Twice Bitten</i> continue the Chicagoland Vampires series's winning streak, it ups the ante.<br /><br />Picking up directly where the second book left off, it's two months after Merit made the change from human to vampire and became the Sentinel of her new house, Cadogan. Although she still struggles - with lust as well as the fighting - during her physical training sessions with House Master Ethan Sullivan, we she her beginning to come into her own. Merit's learning to balance her duties, adjusting to her new life and forming solid relationships with her fellow novitiate (initiated) vampires. She's put her angst over her new-found vampirism aside and seems to be accepting her lot. Her growing level of comfort and her increasing loyalty to her house makes her even more likable - not only for us readers, but also for those novitiates other than her guard co-workers with whom her relations were formerly distant. Despite all of this, Merit still harbors some doubts - doubts that lead to a huge decision that she faces in this installment.<br /><br />Neill does a great job of showing growth in Merit here. Her overall development as a character lends a dose of realism to this paranormal tale, particularly when it comes to her efforts at learning to fight. Urban fantasy series often provide us with heroines that come ready-made to kick ass. It's refreshing to see a heroine make the transition from normal post-grad student to vampire protector. Seeing her succeed is all the more of a reward because of this. In addition, we also witness a wealth of personal growth within Merit. She's more open and honest with herself and others about her feelings, especially those pertaining to Ethan and her unresolved issues with her best friend, Mallory.<br /><br />Ethan too shows some significant growth. It appears as if Merit has tempered his ego and helped him be more forthright emotionally. I came to like Ethan a lot more this time around. Neill managed to make him more sympathetic without straying to far from what we've known of him as a character. I didn't always agree with his decisions or behavior in this book, but I gained a great deal more respect for him. The sexual tension that has simmered between him and Merit since the start jumps off the charts here. Neill takes their relationship in a new direction and I, for one, was surprised at where it went. It provides some lovely conflicts along the way too, and not just between Ethan and Merit. Their relationship issues inevitably spill over into business and are only compounded upon when certain new and returning characters are present in a scene...<br /><br /><a href="http://www.eclecticbooklover.com/2010/06/review-twice-bitten-by-chloe-neill.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Visit my blog, The Eclectic Book Lover, to continue reading this review.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="4972836618862558759" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_95054586" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/95054586" />
    <a title="Alisha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1503257-alisha"><img alt="Alisha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1305444015p2/1503257.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/95054586?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alisha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alisha" href="/user/show/1503257-alisha">Alisha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781101456347" href="/book/show/8519201-twice-bitten">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer95054586" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13943339508412089459">I think Ms. Neill is my kindred author. Or maybe it's that Merit is my kindred protagonist. ^_^ Either way, the Chicagoland Vampires series is definitely at the very top of my "autobuy" list. Not only that, I also find myself obsessed with Merit and her merry band of characters.<br/><br/>For a while though, I was feeling like something was missing from Merit's usual spunky sassiness. Until I realized that it was because for a while, there was no Mallory! They make such a great pair of pals, and bring out </span>
  <span id="freeText13943339508412089459" style="display:none">I think Ms. Neill is my kindred author. Or maybe it's that Merit is my kindred protagonist. ^_^ Either way, the Chicagoland Vampires series is definitely at the very top of my "autobuy" list. Not only that, I also find myself obsessed with Merit and her merry band of characters.<br /><br />For a while though, I was feeling like something was missing from Merit's usual spunky sassiness. Until I realized that it was because for a while, there was no Mallory! They make such a great pair of pals, and bring out the best (and most interesting bits) of each other.<br /><br />The other great pair is of course Merit and Ethan. Sometimes the "will they, won't they" is <i>maddening</i> ^_^...but it sure does keep me glued to the pages. And there are a <i>lot</i> of Ethan-Merit shenanigans in this installment.<br /><br />This book was about three (or maybe 2.5) things. One was the increasing human threat to vampire- (and paranormal-) kind; another is the debate among shifters as to whether to involve themselves in this human threat by continuing to live in secret amongst the population, versus retreating into the Alaskan wilderness. The third theme revolves around Merit's complex feelings and loyalties toward Ethan, and by extension to her house.<br /><br />A couple of my absolute favorite aspects of Neill's storytelling are how comfy her dialogue is and how easy her character interactions are. I swear I loathe having to leave her world behind whenever I finish a book (or even set the book down in-between sessions), and this is in no small part because of how natural everything feels. Paranormal and completely natural, hows about that?<br /><br />Okay, I'd better stop this Chloe Neill-Merit love fest. Just read the book. ^_^ And be aware that you'll likely be itching for the next book immediately upon finishing this one. You've been forewarned.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13943339508412089459" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_101540815" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/101540815" />
    <a title="The Flooze" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/355739-the-flooze"><img alt="The Flooze" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599955192p2/355739.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/101540815?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Flooze" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Flooze" href="/user/show/355739-the-flooze">The Flooze</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/355739-the-flooze?shelf=vanquished_2010">vanquished_2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/355739-the-flooze?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/355739-the-flooze?shelf=urban-fantasy-paranormal">urban-fantasy-paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer101540815" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2450630364504199194">**3.5ish?**<br/><br/>I‘m going against the crowd with this one. <br/><br/>Not fully against, since I do admit that Neill is skilled and that the story is one I'll keep following. However, <i>Twice Bitten</i> (the third book of Chloe Neill’s Chicagoland Vampires series) did not grab me from the get-go. Firstly, too much time was spent on preparations for the shifter convention, leeching away a lot of the adrenaline and tension that should have held center court. Apart from ConPack, the focus rested mainly on character emot</span>
  <span id="freeText2450630364504199194" style="display:none">**3.5ish?**<br /><br />I‘m going against the crowd with this one. <br /><br />Not fully against, since I do admit that Neill is skilled and that the story is one I'll keep following. However, <i>Twice Bitten</i> (the third book of Chloe Neill’s Chicagoland Vampires series) did not grab me from the get-go. Firstly, too much time was spent on preparations for the shifter convention, leeching away a lot of the adrenaline and tension that should have held center court. Apart from ConPack, the focus rested mainly on character emotions and political maneuverings--most of which were either slow to develop, repetitive, or just not engaging enough to hold my interest.<br /><br />Merit can certainly kick ass. She also possesses empathy, plus she can quickly assess a precarious situation down to its component parts and swiftly offer a strategic solution (where she became a master strategist, who knows). In <i>Twice Bitten</i>, she uses these skills to prove herself a valuable asset in diplomatic relations between Cadogan House and the Pack leaders. I like this aspect of her, even if she seems a little too golden-tongued at times. <br /><br />When it comes to her personal life, she's a mess. Her relationship with Ethan is still topsy-turvy and frustrating. At this point, it would benefit from a clear resolution. Maintaining the tension between them led to several exchanges that seemed forced, lessening my desire to see them together once and for all. That said, I did enjoy her handling of oh Lord and Master, Liege of all. She holds her ground and proves she’s not willing to be screwed around. <br /><br />Speaking of that pretty-boy Liege, Ethan seemed off. Granted, he’s emotionally conflicted throughout most of the book so we’re seeing a side of him we haven’t been privy to before. He’s understandably all over the place. However, even his speech patterns varied too widely; several times I read a line I thought belonged to Merit, only to realize it was actually <i>Ethan's</i> comment. The inconsistency in character voice went beyond the normal conversational quirks generally attributed to centuries-old vampires. It irked me and even snatched me out of the flow of the story.<br /><br />Moving along. A lot has been made of Merit and Mallory’s friendship in this series. In the first book, I liked Mal. A sassy friend with her own transformation to bear, she provided a nice touchstone to the human life Merit had to leave behind. Then she got a man, the friends had a fight, and Merit and Mal pushed away from each other. As <i>Twice Bitten</i> began and Merit lamented the damage to their friendship, I suddenly realized something: I didn’t care about their drama. I didn’t give a damn if they ever kissed and made up. When they finally did (at Merit’s convenience), I cared even less. The friendship has moved from a realistic portrayal to one that adds little to the overall story. I hope that Mal’s unique powers come into play further down the road. Otherwise, she’s just someone for Merit to bitch at and have issues with. If that’s the only role Mal is going to play, I’d much rather her friend responsibilities be transferred to Lindsey.<br /><br />With all of this in mind, I was set to assign <i>Twice Bitten</i> a three (entertaining, but flawed/irksome enough that I wouldn’t rush to shove it into friends’ hands). Then the last hundred pages happened. All of a sudden, there was action, suspense, trepidation, miscommunication, and even some conflagration! What was meh became exciting! Don’t you hate when that happens? <br /><br />The revelations of the final chapters and the groundwork they establish for future installments were quite thrilling. They got me keyed up and I’ll be sure to pick up book four of the series. Hopefully, next time around, it won’t take so many pages for Neill to engage me. She’s got fabulous ideas and interesting characters; she just needs to step up her game and make the whole of the story match the thrill of her resolutions.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2450630364504199194" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1864386542" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1864386542" />
    <a title="Treece" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1646176-treece"><img alt="Treece" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579029417p2/1646176.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1864386542?book_show_action=true">Feb 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Treece" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Treece" href="/user/show/1646176-treece">Treece</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/19009654-twice-bitten">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">all PNR lovers</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Treece by: </span>
      me
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1646176-treece?shelf=erotically-inclined">erotically-inclined</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1646176-treece?shelf=hits-the-funny-bone">hits-the-funny-bone</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1646176-treece?shelf=dark-fantasy">dark-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1646176-treece?shelf=teens-to-mils-crowd">teens-to-mils-crowd</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1646176-treece?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1646176-treece?shelf=relationships-baby">relationships-baby</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1646176-treece?shelf=utter-bastard-hero">utter-bastard-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1646176-treece?shelf=abusive-relationship">abusive-relationship</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1646176-treece?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1646176-treece?shelf=cheers-for-underdogs">cheers-for-underdogs</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1864386542" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8298964190054092461">Rating: 5 freakin stars all the way, baby!<br/><br/>This is going to be a short review. Just sayin'<br/><br/>Merit kicks ass. This vamp gal knows how to fight, eat, play, love and party. She is smart in all things except Ethan Sullivan. I know, Merit girl, I know. I feel the same way. It's <i>hard</i>.<br/><br/>Crushing on Gabriel Keene. I know he's married. A reader can dream. <br/><br/>Nick Breckenridge, wonders never cease in good fiction, I tell ya.<br/><br/>Mallory, we are cool again. Love her and Lindsey & the Vamp Crew.<br/><br/>Morgan is still an ass. C</span>
  <span id="freeText8298964190054092461" style="display:none">Rating: 5 freakin stars all the way, baby!<br /><br />This is going to be a short review. Just sayin'<br /><br />Merit kicks ass. This vamp gal knows how to fight, eat, play, love and party. She is smart in all things except Ethan Sullivan. I know, Merit girl, I know. I feel the same way. It's <i>hard</i>.<br /><br />Crushing on Gabriel Keene. I know he's married. A reader can dream. <br /><br />Nick Breckenridge, wonders never cease in good fiction, I tell ya.<br /><br />Mallory, we are cool again. Love her and Lindsey &amp; the Vamp Crew.<br /><br />Morgan is still an ass. Cute, but an ass.<br /><br />I am diggin' Noah. He's hot. <br /><br />*ahem* Where was I? Too much man-crack all over this book. Are there NO ugly shifters and vamps? Dang.<br /><br />Selena, Selena. We're still here, b****. Bring it.<br /><br />Can't wait to see what happens next. This series is long. That's the best part about starting a series later than everyone else.<br /><br />And I finally got to know one of Merit's secrets. Nice.<br /><br />This book was a filler novel but a darned good one. Like your favorite pie filling (fruit or chicken anyone?) Or a layered torte cake with dark chocolate ganache. <br /><br />So many vampires so little time. How can I lose? <br /><br />As for the plot twists, well, I figured out some things (like the surprise in the epilogue) while others were a pleasant and interesting turn.<br /><br />Until then, kids, it's more Chicago Vamps for me.<br /><br />Toodles~<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8298964190054092461" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('om72Rh/T3m5TIMCCAVEaks6dFBW5xPGxEHl+Elp+1zfx1s5ccP5mQ4ja6ns0UqnTrx6Ugnp+IzbYy5J+YsKSlQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sslSBkEEQ0XUtEJ6LsBc45W2QuiG0YgpJU5Q7Li97pThcWocLin7aA9OaIMbw++i9DXCf0VrWq7t/LyAgAGrNg==')})
  }
//]]>

    n = load.length,
    i = 0,
    go = function () {
      for (i = 0; i < n; i += 1) {
        script = d.createElement('SCRIPT');
        script.type = 'text/javascript';
        script.async = true;
        script.src = load[i];
        first.parentNode.insertBefore(script, first);
      }
    }
  if (w.attachEvent) {
    w.attachEvent('onload', go);
  } else {
    w.addEventListener('load', go, false);
  }
}(window, document,
    ['//assets.pinterest.com/js/pinit.js',
     '//apis.google.com/js/plusone.js'
    ]
  ));

//]]>
</script>
